### (43/51 | 43/258) Edisum: Summarizing and Explaining Wikipedia Edits at Scale (Marija Šakota et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Marija Šakota, Isaac Johnson, Guosheng Feng, Robert West. (2024)  
**Edisum: Summarizing and Explaining Wikipedia Edits at Scale**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Edisum: Summarizing and Explaining Wikipedia Edits at Scale" index=43>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-43 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.CL  
Categories: cs-CL, cs.CL  
Keyword Score: 20  
Keywords: Fine-tuning, Large Language Model  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03428v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03428v1.pdf" filename="2404.03428v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
An edit summary is a succinct comment written by a Wikipedia editor explaining the nature of, and reasons for, an edit to a Wikipedia page. Edit summaries are crucial for maintaining the encyclopedia: they are the first thing seen by content moderators and help them decide whether to accept or reject an edit. Additionally, edit summaries constitute a valuable data source for researchers. Unfortunately, as we show, for many edits, summaries are either missing or incomplete. To overcome this problem and help editors write useful edit summaries, we propose a model for recommending edit summaries generated by a language model trained to produce good edit summaries given the representation of an edit diff. This is a challenging task for multiple reasons, including mixed-quality training data, the need to understand not only what was changed in the article but also why it was changed, and efficiency requirements imposed by the scale of Wikipedia. We address these challenges by curating a mix of human and synthetically generated training data and <b>fine-tuning</b> a generative language model sufficiently small to be used on Wikipedia at scale. Our model performs on par with human editors. Commercial <b>large</b> <b>language</b> <b>models</b> are able to solve this task better than human editors, but would be too expensive to run on Wikipedia at scale. More broadly, this paper showcases how language modeling technology can be used to support humans in maintaining one of the largest and most visible projects on the Web.

{{</citation>}}

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03302v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
By leveraging the retrieval of information from external knowledge databases, <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> <b>(LLMs)</b> exhibit enhanced capabilities for accomplishing many knowledge-intensive tasks. However, due to the inherent flaws of current retrieval systems, there might exist irrelevant information within those retrieving top-ranked passages. In this work, we present a comprehensive investigation into the robustness of <b>LLMs</b> to different types of irrelevant information under various conditions. We initially introduce a framework to construct high-quality irrelevant information that ranges from semantically unrelated, partially related, and related to questions. Furthermore, our analysis demonstrates that the constructed irrelevant information not only scores highly on similarity metrics, being highly retrieved by existing systems, but also bears semantic connections to the context. Our investigation reveals that current <b>LLMs</b> still face challenges in discriminating highly semantically related information and can be easily distracted by these irrelevant yet misleading contents. Besides, we also find that current solutions for handling irrelevant information have limitations in improving the robustness of <b>LLMs</b> to such distractions. Resources are available at https://github.com/Di-viner/LLM-Robustness-to-Irrelevant-Information.

**Language Model Evolution: An Iterated Learning Perspective**

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.04286v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>

**ABSTRACT**  
With the widespread adoption of <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> <b>(LLMs),</b> the prevalence of iterative interactions among these models is anticipated to increase. We draw parallels between the behavior of <b>LLMs</b> and the evolution of human culture, as the latter has been extensively studied by cognitive scientists for decades. Our approach involves leveraging Iterated Learning (IL), a Bayesian framework that elucidates how subtle biases are magnified during human cultural evolution, to explain some behaviors of <b>LLMs.</b> This paper outlines key characteristics of agents' behavior in the Bayesian-IL framework, including predictions that are supported by experimental verification with various <b>LLMs.</b> This theoretical framework could help to more effectively predict and guide the evolution of <b>LLMs</b> in desired directions.

### (48/51 | 48/258) Evaluating Document Simplification: On the Importance of Separately Assessing Simplicity and Meaning Preservation (Liam Cripwell et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Liam Cripwell, Joël Legrand, Claire Gardent. (2024)  
**Evaluating Document Simplification: On the Importance of Separately Assessing Simplicity and Meaning Preservation**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Evaluating Document Simplification: On the Importance of Separately Assessing Simplicity and Meaning Preservation" index=48>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-48 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">

---
Primary Category: cs.CL  
Categories: cs-CL, cs.CL  
Keyword Score: 10  
Keywords: BERTScore  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03278v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03278v1.pdf" filename="2404.03278v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Text simplification intends to make a text easier to read while preserving its core meaning. Intuitively and as shown in previous works, these two dimensions (simplification and meaning preservation) are often-times inversely correlated. An overly conservative text will fail to simplify sufficiently, whereas extreme simplification will degrade meaning preservation. Yet, popular evaluation metrics either aggregate meaning preservation and simplification into a single score (SARI, LENS), or target meaning preservation alone <b>(BERTScore,</b> QuestEval). Moreover, these metrics usually require a set of references and most previous work has only focused on sentence-level simplification. In this paper, we focus on the evaluation of document-level text simplification and compare existing models using distinct metrics for meaning preservation and simplification. We leverage existing metrics from similar tasks and introduce a reference-less metric variant for simplicity, showing that models are mostly biased towards either simplification or meaning preservation, seldom performing well on both dimensions. Making use of the fact that the metrics we use are all reference-less, we also investigate the performance of existing models when applied to unseen data (where reference simplifications are unavailable).

{{</citation>}}

**ABSTRACT**  
With the rise of computational social science, many scholars utilize data analysis and natural language processing tools to analyze social media, news articles, and other accessible data sources for examining political and social discourse. We demonstrate that the application of <b>knowledge</b> <b>representation</b> techniques to the aforementioned news streams highlights, contrary to common assumptions, shows relative "internal" neutrality of both sources and polarizing attitude towards a small fraction of entities. Additionally, we argue that such characteristics in information sources lead to fundamental disparities in audience worldviews, potentially acting as a catalyst for the formation of echo-chambers.

### (51/51 | 51/258) M3TCM: Multi-modal Multi-task Context Model for Utterance Classification in Motivational Interviews (Sayed Muddashir Hossain et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Sayed Muddashir Hossain, Jan Alexandersson, Philipp Müller. (2024)  
**M3TCM: Multi-modal Multi-task Context Model for Utterance Classification in Motivational Interviews**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="M3TCM: Multi-modal Multi-task Context Model for Utterance Classification in Motivational Interviews" index=51>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-51 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>

---
Primary Category: cs.CL  
Categories: cs-CL, cs-SD, cs.CL, eess-AS

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03312v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03312v1.pdf" filename="2404.03312v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Accurate utterance classification in motivational interviews is crucial to automatically understand the quality and dynamics of client-therapist interaction, and it can serve as a key input for systems mediating such interactions. Motivational interviews exhibit three important characteristics. First, there are two distinct roles, namely client and therapist. Second, they are often highly emotionally charged, which can be expressed both in text and in prosody. Finally, context is of central importance to classify any given utterance. Previous works did not adequately incorporate all of these characteristics into utterance classification approaches for mental health dialogues. In contrast, we present M3TCM, a <b>Multi-modal,</b> Multi-task Context Model for utterance classification. Our approach for the first time employs multi-task learning to effectively model both joint and individual components of therapist and client behaviour. Furthermore, M3TCM integrates information from the text and speech modality as well as the conversation context. With our novel approach, we outperform the state of the art for utterance classification on the recently introduced AnnoMI dataset with a relative improvement of 20% for the client- and by 15% for therapist utterance classification. In extensive ablation studies, we quantify the improvement resulting from each contribution.

### (1/8 | 52/258) A Comprehensive Survey on Self-Supervised Learning for Recommendation (Xubin Ren et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Xubin Ren, Wei Wei, Lianghao Xia, Chao Huang. (2024)  
**A Comprehensive Survey on Self-Supervised Learning for Recommendation**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="A Comprehensive Survey on Self-Supervised Learning for Recommendation" index=52>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-52 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.IR  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-IR, cs.IR  
Keyword Score: 110  
Keywords: Graph Neural Network, Adversarial Learning, Contrastive Learning, Recommendation, Recommender System, Self-supervised Learning, Self-supervised Learning, Supervised Learning, Supervised Learning, Recurrent Neural Network, Transformer  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03354v2" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03354v2.pdf" filename="2404.03354v2.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Recommender</b> <b>systems</b> play a crucial role in tackling the challenge of information overload by delivering personalized <b>recommendations</b> based on individual user preferences. Deep learning techniques, such as <b>RNNs,</b> <b>GNNs,</b> and <b>Transformer</b> architectures, have significantly propelled the advancement of <b>recommender</b> <b>systems</b> by enhancing their comprehension of user behaviors and preferences. However, <b>supervised</b> <b>learning</b> methods encounter challenges in real-life scenarios due to data sparsity, resulting in limitations in their ability to learn representations effectively. To address this, <b>self-supervised</b> <b>learning</b> (SSL) techniques have emerged as a solution, leveraging inherent data structures to generate supervision signals without relying solely on labeled data. By leveraging unlabeled data and extracting meaningful representations, <b>recommender</b> <b>systems</b> utilizing SSL can make accurate predictions and <b>recommendations</b> even when confronted with data sparsity. In this paper, we provide a comprehensive review of <b>self-supervised</b> <b>learning</b> frameworks designed for <b>recommender</b> <b>systems,</b> encompassing a thorough analysis of over 170 papers. We conduct an exploration of nine distinct scenarios, enabling a comprehensive understanding of SSL-enhanced <b>recommenders</b> <b>in</b> different contexts. For each domain, we elaborate on different <b>self-supervised</b> <b>learning</b> paradigms, namely <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning,</b> generative learning, and <b>adversarial</b> <b>learning,</b> so as to present technical details of how SSL enhances <b>recommender</b> <b>systems</b> in various contexts. We consistently maintain the related open-source materials at https://github.com/HKUDS/Awesome-SSLRec-Papers.

{{</citation>}}


### (2/8 | 53/258) Do Large Language Models Rank Fairly? An Empirical Study on the Fairness of LLMs as Rankers (Yuan Wang et al., 2024)

**Do Large Language Models Rank Fairly? An Empirical Study on the Fairness of LLMs as Rankers**

**ABSTRACT**  
The integration of <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> <b>(LLMs)</b> in <b>information</b> <b>retrieval</b> has raised a critical reevaluation of <b>fairness</b> in the text-ranking models. <b>LLMs,</b> such as <b>GPT</b> models and Llama2, have shown effectiveness in <b>natural</b> <b>language</b> <b>understanding</b> tasks, and prior works (e.g., RankGPT) have also demonstrated that the <b>LLMs</b> exhibit better performance than the traditional ranking models in the ranking task. However, their <b>fairness</b> remains largely unexplored. This paper presents an empirical study evaluating these <b>LLMs</b> using the TREC Fair Ranking dataset, focusing on the representation of binary protected attributes such as gender and geographic location, which are historically underrepresented in search outcomes. Our analysis delves into how these <b>LLMs</b> handle queries and documents related to these attributes, aiming to uncover biases in their ranking algorithms. We assess <b>fairness</b> from both user and content perspectives, contributing an empirical <b>benchmark</b> for evaluating <b>LLMs</b> as the fair ranker.

{{</citation>}}

**ABSTRACT**  
The emergence of <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> <b>(LLMs)</b> has achieved tremendous success in the field of Natural Language Processing owing to diverse training paradigms that empower <b>LLMs</b> to effectively capture intricate linguistic patterns and semantic representations. In particular, the recent "pre-train, <b>prompt</b> and predict" training paradigm has attracted significant attention as an approach for learning generalizable models with limited labeled data. In line with this advancement, these training paradigms have recently been adapted to the <b>recommendation</b> domain and are seen as a promising direction in both academia and industry. This half-day tutorial aims to provide a thorough understanding of extracting and transferring knowledge from pre-trained models learned through different training paradigms to improve <b>recommender</b> <b>systems</b> from various perspectives, such as generality, sparsity, effectiveness and trustworthiness. In this tutorial, we first introduce the basic concepts and a generic architecture of the language modeling paradigm for <b>recommendation</b> purposes. Then, we focus on recent advancements in adapting <b>LLM-related</b> training strategies and optimization objectives for different <b>recommendation</b> tasks. After that, we will systematically introduce ethical issues in <b>LLM-based</b> <b>recommender</b> <b>systems</b> and discuss possible approaches to assessing and mitigating them. We will also <b>summarize</b> the relevant datasets, evaluation metrics, and an empirical study on the <b>recommendation</b> performance of training paradigms. Finally, we will conclude the tutorial with a discussion of open challenges and future directions.

{{</citation>}}


### (4/8 | 55/258) Sequential Recommendation for Optimizing Both Immediate Feedback and Long-term Retention (Ziru Liu et al., 2024)

**Sequential Recommendation for Optimizing Both Immediate Feedback and Long-term Retention**

Primary Category: cs.IR

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03637v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03637v1.pdf" filename="2404.03637v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

**ABSTRACT**  
In the landscape of <b>Recommender</b> <b>System</b> (RS) applications, <b>reinforcement</b> <b>learning</b> (RL) has recently emerged as a powerful tool, primarily due to its proficiency in optimizing long-term rewards. Nevertheless, it suffers from instability in the learning process, <b>stemming</b> from the intricate interactions among bootstrapping, off-policy training, and function approximation. Moreover, in multi-reward <b>recommendation</b> scenarios, designing a proper reward setting that reconciles the inner dynamics of various tasks is quite intricate. In response to these challenges, we introduce DT4IER, an advanced decision <b>transformer-based</b> <b>recommendation</b> model that is engineered to not only elevate the effectiveness of <b>recommendations</b> but also to achieve a harmonious balance between immediate user engagement and long-term retention. The DT4IER applies an innovative multi-reward design that adeptly balances short and long-term rewards with user-specific attributes, which serve to enhance the contextual richness of the reward sequence ensuring a more informed and personalized <b>recommendation</b> process. To enhance its predictive capabilities, DT4IER incorporates a high-dimensional encoder, skillfully designed to identify and leverage the intricate interrelations across diverse tasks. Furthermore, we integrate a <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning</b> approach within the action embedding predictions, a strategy that significantly boosts the model's overall performance. Experiments on three real-world datasets demonstrate the effectiveness of DT4IER against state-of-the-art Sequential <b>Recommender</b> <b>Systems</b> (SRSs) and Multi-Task Learning (MTL) models in terms of both prediction accuracy and effectiveness in specific tasks. The source code is accessible online to facilitate replication

{{</citation>}}


### (5/8 | 56/258) A Directional Diffusion Graph Transformer for Recommendation (Zixuan Yi et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Zixuan Yi, Xi Wang, Iadh Ounis. (2024)  
**A Directional Diffusion Graph Transformer for Recommendation**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="A Directional Diffusion Graph Transformer for Recommendation" index=56>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-56 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.IR  
Categories: cs-IR, cs.IR  
Keyword Score: 46  
Keywords: Diffusion Model, Graph, Benchmarking, Recommendation, Recommender System, Transformer  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03326v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03326v1.pdf" filename="2404.03326v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
In real-world <b>recommender</b> <b>systems,</b> implicitly collected user feedback, while abundant, often includes noisy false-positive and false-negative interactions. The possible misinterpretations of the user-item interactions pose a significant challenge for traditional <b>graph</b> neural <b>recommenders.</b> <b>These</b> approaches aggregate the users' or items' neighbours based on implicit user-item interactions in order to accurately capture the users' profiles. To account for and model possible noise in the users' interactions in <b>graph</b> neural <b>recommenders,</b> <b>we</b> propose a novel <b>Diffusion</b> <b>Graph</b> <b>Transformer</b> (DiffGT) model for top-k <b>recommendation.</b> Our DiffGT model employs a <b>diffusion</b> <b>process,</b> which includes a forward phase for gradually introducing noise to implicit interactions, followed by a reverse process to iteratively refine the representations of the users' hidden preferences (i.e., a denoising process). In our proposed approach, given the inherent anisotropic structure observed in the user-item interaction <b>graph,</b> we specifically use anisotropic and directional Gaussian noises in the forward <b>diffusion</b> <b>process.</b> Our approach differs from the sole use of isotropic Gaussian noises in existing <b>diffusion</b> <b>models.</b> In the reverse <b>diffusion</b> <b>process,</b> to reverse the effect of noise added earlier and recover the true users' preferences, we integrate a <b>graph</b> <b>transformer</b> architecture with a linear attention module to denoise the noisy user/item embeddings in an effective and efficient manner. In addition, such a reverse <b>diffusion</b> <b>process</b> is further guided by personalised information (e.g., interacted items) to enable the accurate estimation of the users' preferences on items. Our extensive experiments conclusively demonstrate the superiority of our proposed <b>graph</b> <b>diffusion</b> <b>model</b> over ten existing state-of-the-art approaches across three <b>benchmark</b> datasets.

{{</citation>}}


### (6/8 | 57/258) GenQREnsemble: Zero-Shot LLM Ensemble Prompting for Generative Query Reformulation (Kaustubh Dhole et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Kaustubh Dhole, Eugene Agichtein. (2024)  
**GenQREnsemble: Zero-Shot LLM Ensemble Prompting for Generative Query Reformulation**
<br/>

<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-57 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">

Primary Category: cs.IR

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03746v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Query Reformulation(QR) is a set of techniques used to transform a user's original search query to a text that better aligns with the user's intent and improves their search experience. Recently, <b>zero-shot</b> QR has been shown to be a promising approach due to its ability to exploit knowledge inherent in <b>large</b> <b>language</b> <b>models.</b> By taking inspiration from the success of ensemble <b>prompting</b> strategies which have benefited many tasks, we investigate if they can help improve query reformulation. In this context, we propose an ensemble based <b>prompting</b> technique, GenQREnsemble which leverages paraphrases of a <b>zero-shot</b> instruction to generate multiple sets of keywords ultimately improving retrieval performance. We further introduce its post-retrieval variant, GenQREnsembleRF to incorporate pseudo relevant feedback. On evaluations over four IR <b>benchmarks,</b> we find that GenQREnsemble generates better reformulations with relative nDCG@10 improvements up to 18% and MAP improvements upto 24% over the previous <b>zero-shot</b> state-of-art. On the MSMarco Passage Ranking task, GenQREnsembleRF shows relative gains of 5% MRR using pseudo-relevance feedback, and 9% nDCG@10 using relevant feedback documents.

{{</citation>}}

Haonan Zhang, Dongxia Wang, Zhu Sun, Yanhui Li, Youcheng Sun, Huizhi Liang, Wenhai Wang. (2024)  
**Does Knowledge Graph Really Matter for Recommender Systems?**

  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>

---
Primary Category: cs.IR  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-IR, cs-LG, cs.IR  
Keyword Score: 33  
Keywords: Graph, Knowledge Graph, Knowledge Graph, Recommendation, Recommender System  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03164v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03164v1.pdf" filename="2404.03164v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Recommender</b> <b>systems</b> (RSs) are designed to provide personalized <b>recommendations</b> to users. Recently, <b>knowledge</b> <b>graphs</b> <b>(KGs)</b> have been widely introduced in RSs to improve <b>recommendation</b> accuracy. In this study, however, we demonstrate that RSs do not necessarily perform worse even if the <b>KG</b> is downgraded to the user-item interaction <b>graph</b> only (or removed). We propose an evaluation framework KG4RecEval to systematically evaluate how much a <b>KG</b> contributes to the <b>recommendation</b> accuracy of a <b>KG-based</b> RS, using our defined metric KGER <b>(KG</b> utilization efficiency in <b>recommendation).</b> We consider the scenarios where <b>knowledge</b> <b>in</b> a <b>KG</b> gets completely removed, randomly distorted and decreased, and also where <b>recommendations</b> are for cold-start users. Our extensive experiments on four commonly used datasets and a number of state-of-the-art <b>KG-based</b> RSs reveal that: to remove, randomly distort or decrease <b>knowledge</b> <b>does</b> not necessarily decrease <b>recommendation</b> accuracy, even for cold-start users. These findings inspire us to rethink how to better utilize <b>knowledge</b> <b>from</b> existing <b>KGs,</b> whereby we discuss and provide insights into what characteristics of datasets and <b>KG-based</b> RSs may help improve <b>KG</b> utilization efficiency.

{{</citation>}}


### (8/8 | 59/258) To Search or to Recommend: Predicting Open-App Motivation with Neural Hawkes Process (Zhongxiang Sun et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Zhongxiang Sun, Zihua Si, Xiao Zhang, Xiaoxue Zang, Yang Song, Hongteng Xu, Jun Xu. (2024)  
**To Search or to Recommend: Predicting Open-App Motivation with Neural Hawkes Process**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="To Search or to Recommend: Predicting Open-App Motivation with Neural Hawkes Process" index=59>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-59 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">

---
Primary Category: cs.IR  
Categories: cs-IR, cs.IR  
Keyword Score: 23  
Keywords: Benchmarking, Recommendation, Transformer  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03267v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03267v1.pdf" filename="2404.03267v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Incorporating Search and <b>Recommendation</b> (S&R) services within a singular application is prevalent in online platforms, leading to a new task termed open-app motivation prediction, which aims to predict whether users initiate the application with the specific intent of information searching, or to explore recommended content for entertainment. Studies have shown that predicting users' motivation to open an app can help to improve user engagement and enhance performance in various downstream tasks. However, accurately predicting open-app motivation is not trivial, as it is influenced by user-specific factors, search queries, clicked items, as well as their temporal occurrences. Furthermore, these activities occur sequentially and exhibit intricate temporal dependencies. Inspired by the success of the Neural Hawkes Process (NHP) in modeling temporal dependencies in sequences, this paper proposes a novel neural Hawkes process model to capture the temporal dependencies between historical user browsing and querying actions. The model, referred to as Neural Hawkes Process-based Open-App Motivation prediction model (NHP-OAM), employs a hierarchical <b>transformer</b> and a novel intensity function to encode multiple factors, and open-app motivation prediction layer to integrate time and user-specific information for predicting users' open-app motivations. To demonstrate the superiority of our NHP-OAM model and construct a <b>benchmark</b> for the Open-App Motivation Prediction task, we not only extend the public S&R dataset ZhihuRec but also construct a new real-world Open-App Motivation Dataset (OAMD). Experiments on these two datasets validate NHP-OAM's superiority over baseline models. Further downstream application experiments demonstrate NHP-OAM's effectiveness in predicting users' Open-App Motivation, highlighting the immense application value of NHP-OAM.

{{</citation>}}

### (1/44 | 60/258) Direct Nash Optimization: Teaching Language Models to Self-Improve with General Preferences (Corby Rosset et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Corby Rosset, Ching-An Cheng, Arindam Mitra, Michael Santacroce, Ahmed Awadallah, Tengyang Xie. (2024)  
**Direct Nash Optimization: Teaching Language Models to Self-Improve with General Preferences**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Direct Nash Optimization: Teaching Language Models to Self-Improve with General Preferences" index=60>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-60 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-CL, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 100  
Keywords: Contrastive Learning, Reinforcement Learning, Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback, Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback, GPT, GPT-4, GPT-4 turbo, Mistral, Large Language Model, Large Language Model  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03715v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03715v1.pdf" filename="2404.03715v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
This paper studies post-training <b>large</b> <b>language</b> <b>models</b> <b>(LLMs)</b> using preference feedback from a powerful oracle to help a model iteratively improve over itself. The typical approach for post-training <b>LLMs</b> involves <b>Reinforcement</b> <b>Learning</b> <b>from</b> <b>Human</b> <b>Feedback</b> <b>(RLHF),</b> which traditionally separates reward learning and subsequent policy optimization. However, such a reward maximization approach is limited by the nature of "point-wise" rewards (such as Bradley-Terry model), which fails to express complex intransitive or cyclic preference relations. While advances on <b>RLHF</b> show reward learning and policy optimization can be merged into a single <b>contrastive</b> <b>objective</b> for stability, they yet still remain tethered to the reward maximization framework. Recently, a new wave of research sidesteps the reward maximization presumptions in favor of directly optimizing over "pair-wise" or general preferences. In this paper, we introduce Direct Nash Optimization (DNO), a provable and scalable algorithm that marries the simplicity and stability of <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning</b> with theoretical generality from optimizing general preferences. Because DNO is a batched on-policy algorithm using a regression-based objective, its implementation is straightforward and efficient. Moreover, DNO enjoys monotonic improvement across iterations that help it improve even over a strong teacher (such as <b>GPT-4).</b> <b>In</b> our experiments, a resulting 7B parameter Orca-2.5 model aligned by DNO achieves the state-of-the-art win-rate against <b>GPT-4-Turbo</b> <b>of</b> 33% on AlpacaEval 2.0 (even after controlling for response length), an absolute gain of 26% (7% to 33%) over the initializing model. It outperforms models with far more parameters, including <b>Mistral</b> <b>Large,</b> <b>Self-Rewarding</b> <b>LM</b> (70B parameters), and older versions of <b>GPT-4.</b>

{{</citation>}}


### (2/44 | 61/258) Knowledge Distillation-Based Model Extraction Attack using Private Counterfactual Explanations (Fatima Ezzeddine et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Fatima Ezzeddine, Omran Ayoub, Silvia Giordano. (2024)  
**Knowledge Distillation-Based Model Extraction Attack using Private Counterfactual Explanations**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Knowledge Distillation-Based Model Extraction Attack using Private Counterfactual Explanations" index=61>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-61 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-CR, cs-CY, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 90  
Keywords: Counter-factual, Explainable AI, Generative Adversarial Network, Generative Adversarial Network, Knowledge Distillation, Knowledge Distillation, Knowledge Distillation, Differential Privacy, Model Extraction  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03348v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03348v1.pdf" filename="2404.03348v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
In recent years, there has been a notable increase in the deployment of machine learning (ML) <b>models</b> <b>as</b> services (MLaaS) across diverse production software applications. In parallel, <b>explainable</b> <b>AI</b> (XAI) continues to evolve, addressing the necessity for transparency and trustworthiness in ML <b>models.</b> <b>XAI</b> techniques aim to enhance the transparency of ML <b>models</b> <b>by</b> providing insights, in terms of the <b>model's</b> <b>explanations,</b> into their decision-making process. Simultaneously, some MLaaS platforms now offer explanations alongside the ML prediction outputs. This setup has elevated concerns regarding vulnerabilities in MLaaS, particularly in relation to privacy leakage attacks such as <b>model</b> <b>extraction</b> attacks (MEA). This is due to the fact that explanations can unveil insights about the inner workings of the <b>model</b> <b>which</b> could be exploited by malicious users. In this work, we focus on investigating how <b>model</b> <b>explanations,</b> particularly <b>Generative</b> <b>adversarial</b> <b>networks</b> <b>(GANs)-based</b> <b>counterfactual</b> explanations (CFs), can be exploited for performing MEA within the MLaaS platform. We also delve into assessing the effectiveness of incorporating <b>differential</b> <b>privacy</b> (DP) as a mitigation strategy. To this end, we first propose a novel MEA methodology based on <b>Knowledge</b> <b>Distillation</b> <b>(KD)</b> to enhance the efficiency of extracting a substitute <b>model</b> <b>of</b> a target <b>model</b> <b>exploiting</b> CFs. Then, we advise an approach for training CF generators incorporating DP to generate private CFs. We conduct thorough experimental evaluations on real-world datasets and demonstrate that our proposed <b>KD-based</b> MEA can yield a high-fidelity substitute <b>model</b> <b>with</b> reduced queries with respect to baseline approaches. Furthermore, our findings reveal that the inclusion of a privacy layer impacts the performance of the explainer, the quality of CFs, and results in a reduction in the MEA performance.

{{</citation>}}


### (3/44 | 62/258) On the Surprising Efficacy of Distillation as an Alternative to Pre-Training Small Models (Sean Farhat et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Sean Farhat, Deming Chen. (2024)  
**On the Surprising Efficacy of Distillation as an Alternative to Pre-Training Small Models**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="On the Surprising Efficacy of Distillation as an Alternative to Pre-Training Small Models" index=62>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-62 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 80  
Keywords: Contrastive Learning, Convolution, Fine-tuning, Knowledge Distillation, Knowledge Distillation, Knowledge Distillation, Transformer, Prompt  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03263v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03263v1.pdf" filename="2404.03263v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
In this paper, we propose that small models may not need to absorb the cost of pre-training to reap its benefits. Instead, they can capitalize on the astonishing results achieved by modern, enormous models to a surprising degree. We observe that, when <b>distilled</b> on a task from a pre-trained teacher model, a small model can achieve or surpass the performance it would achieve if it was pre-trained then <b>finetuned</b> on that task. To allow this phenomenon to be easily leveraged, we establish a connection reducing <b>knowledge</b> <b>distillation</b> to modern <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning,</b> opening two doors: (1) vastly different model architecture pairings can work for the <b>distillation,</b> and (2) most <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning</b> algorithms rooted in the theory of Noise <b>Contrastive</b> <b>Estimation</b> can be easily applied and used. We demonstrate this paradigm using pre-trained teacher models from open-source model hubs, <b>Transformer</b> and <b>convolution</b> based model combinations, and a novel <b>distillation</b> algorithm that massages the Alignment/Uniformity perspective of <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning</b> by Wang & Isola (2020) into a <b>distillation</b> objective. We choose this flavor of <b>contrastive</b> <b>learning</b> due to its low computational cost, an overarching theme of this work. We also observe that this phenomenon tends not to occur if the task is data-limited. However, this can be alleviated by leveraging yet another scale-inspired development: large, pre-trained generative models for dataset augmentation. Again, we use an open-source model, and our rudimentary <b>prompts</b> are sufficient to boost the small model`s performance. Thus, we highlight a training method for small models that is up to 94% faster than the standard pre-training paradigm without sacrificing performance. For practitioners discouraged from fully utilizing modern foundation datasets for their small models due to the prohibitive scale, we believe our work keeps that door open.

{{</citation>}}


### (4/44 | 63/258) Investigating Regularization of Self-Play Language Models (Reda Alami et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Reda Alami, Abdalgader Abubaker, Mastane Achab, Mohamed El Amine Seddik, Salem Lahlou. (2024)  
**Investigating Regularization of Self-Play Language Models**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Investigating Regularization of Self-Play Language Models" index=63>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-63 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 70  
Keywords: Direct Preference Optimization, Fine-tuning, Reinforcement Learning, Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback, Reinforcement Learning from Human Feedback, Neural Machine Translation, Large Language Model  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.04291v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.04291v1.pdf" filename="2404.04291v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
This paper explores the effects of various forms of regularization in the context of language model alignment via self-play. While both <b>reinforcement</b> <b>learning</b> <b>from</b> <b>human</b> <b>feedback</b> <b>(RLHF)</b> and <b>direct</b> <b>preference</b> <b>optimization</b> (DPO) require to collect costly human-annotated pairwise preferences, the self-play <b>fine-tuning</b> (SPIN) approach replaces the rejected answers by data generated from the previous iterate. However, the SPIN method presents a performance instability issue in the learning phase, which can be mitigated by playing against a mixture of the two previous iterates. In the same vein, we propose in this work to address this issue from two perspectives: first, by incorporating an additional Kullback-Leibler (KL) regularization to stay at the proximity of the reference policy; second, by using the idea of fictitious play which smoothens the opponent policy across all previous iterations. In particular, we show that the KL-based regularizer boils down to replacing the previous policy by its geometric mixture with the base policy inside of the SPIN loss function. We finally discuss empirical results on <b>MT-Bench</b> as well as on the Hugging Face Open <b>LLM</b> Leaderboard.

{{</citation>}}


### (5/44 | 64/258) Red Teaming GPT-4V: Are GPT-4V Safe Against Uni/Multi-Modal Jailbreak Attacks? (Shuo Chen et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Shuo Chen, Zhen Han, Bailan He, Zifeng Ding, Wenqian Yu, Philip Torr, Volker Tresp, Jindong Gu. (2024)  
**Red Teaming GPT-4V: Are GPT-4V Safe Against Uni/Multi-Modal Jailbreak Attacks?**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Red Teaming GPT-4V: Are GPT-4V Safe Against Uni/Multi-Modal Jailbreak Attacks?" index=64>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-64 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-CL, cs-CR, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 49  
Keywords: Benchmarking, Multi-modal, Multi-modal, GPT, GPT-4, Large Language Model, Large Language Model  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03411v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03411v1.pdf" filename="2404.03411v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Various jailbreak attacks have been proposed to red-team <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> <b>(LLMs)</b> and revealed the vulnerable safeguards of <b>LLMs.</b> Besides, some methods are not limited to the textual modality and extend the jailbreak attack to <b>Multimodal</b> <b>Large</b> <b>Language</b> <b>Models</b> (MLLMs) by perturbing the visual input. However, the absence of a universal evaluation <b>benchmark</b> complicates the performance reproduction and fair comparison. Besides, there is a lack of comprehensive evaluation of closed-source state-of-the-art (SOTA) models, especially MLLMs, such as <b>GPT-4V.</b> To address these issues, this work first builds a comprehensive jailbreak evaluation dataset with 1445 harmful questions covering 11 different safety policies. Based on this dataset, extensive red-teaming experiments are conducted on 11 different <b>LLMs</b> and MLLMs, including both SOTA proprietary models and open-source models. We then conduct a deep analysis of the evaluated results and find that (1) <b>GPT4</b> and <b>GPT-4V</b> demonstrate better robustness against jailbreak attacks compared to open-source <b>LLMs</b> and MLLMs. (2) Llama2 and Qwen-VL-Chat are more robust compared to other open-source models. (3) The transferability of visual jailbreak methods is relatively limited compared to textual jailbreak methods. The dataset and code can be found here https://anonymous.4open.science/r/red_teaming_gpt4-C1CE/README.md .

{{</citation>}}


### (6/44 | 65/258) Theoretical and Empirical Insights into the Origins of Degree Bias in Graph Neural Networks (Arjun Subramonian et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Arjun Subramonian, Jian Kang, Yizhou Sun. (2024)  
**Theoretical and Empirical Insights into the Origins of Degree Bias in Graph Neural Networks**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Theoretical and Empirical Insights into the Origins of Degree Bias in Graph Neural Networks" index=65>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-65 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-LG, cs-SI, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 43  
Keywords: Message-Passing, Node Classification, Graph, Graph Neural Network, Graph Neural Network  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03139v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03139v1.pdf" filename="2404.03139v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Graph</b> <b>Neural</b> <b>Networks</b> <b>(GNNs)</b> often perform better for high-degree <b>nodes</b> <b>than</b> low-degree <b>nodes</b> <b>on</b> <b>node</b> <b>classification</b> tasks. This degree bias can reinforce social marginalization by, e.g., sidelining authors of lowly-cited papers when predicting paper topics in citation networks. While researchers have proposed numerous hypotheses for why <b>GNN</b> degree bias occurs, we find via a survey of 38 degree bias papers that these hypotheses are often not rigorously validated, and can even be contradictory. Thus, we provide an analysis of the origins of degree bias in <b>message-passing</b> <b>GNNs</b> with different <b>graph</b> <b>filters.</b> <b>We</b> prove that high-degree test <b>nodes</b> <b>tend</b> to have a lower probability of misclassification regardless of how <b>GNNs</b> are trained. Moreover, we show that degree bias arises from a variety of factors that are associated with a <b>node's</b> <b>degree</b> (e.g., homophily of neighbors, diversity of neighbors). Furthermore, we show that during training, some <b>GNNs</b> may adjust their loss on low-degree <b>nodes</b> <b>more</b> slowly than on high-degree <b>nodes;</b> <b>however,</b> with sufficiently many epochs of training, <b>message-passing</b> <b>GNNs</b> can achieve their maximum possible training accuracy, which is not significantly limited by their expressive power. Throughout our analysis, we connect our findings to previously-proposed hypotheses for the origins of degree bias, supporting and unifying some while drawing doubt to others. We validate our theoretical findings on 8 common real-world networks, and based on our theoretical and empirical insights, describe a roadmap to alleviate degree bias.

{{</citation>}}


### (7/44 | 66/258) Learning Social Fairness Preferences from Non-Expert Stakeholder Opinions in Kidney Placement (Mukund Telukunta et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Mukund Telukunta, Sukruth Rao, Gabriella Stickney, Venkata Sriram Siddardh Nadendla, Casey Canfield. (2024)  
**Learning Social Fairness Preferences from Non-Expert Stakeholder Opinions in Kidney Placement**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Learning Social Fairness Preferences from Non-Expert Stakeholder Opinions in Kidney Placement" index=66>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>

Primary Category: cs.LG

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03800v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03800v1.pdf" filename="2404.03800v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Modern kidney placement incorporates several intelligent <b>recommendation</b> systems which exhibit social discrimination due to biases inherited from training data. Although initial attempts were made in the literature to study algorithmic <b>fairness</b> in kidney placement, these methods replace true outcomes with surgeons' decisions due to the long delays involved in recording such outcomes reliably. However, the replacement of true outcomes with surgeons' decisions disregards expert stakeholders' biases as well as social opinions of other stakeholders who do not possess medical expertise. This paper alleviates the latter concern and designs a novel <b>fairness</b> feedback survey to evaluate an acceptance rate predictor (ARP) that predicts a kidney's acceptance rate in a given kidney-match pair. The survey is launched on Prolific, a crowdsourcing platform, and public opinions are collected from 85 anonymous crowd participants. A novel social <b>fairness</b> preference learning algorithm is proposed based on minimizing social feedback regret computed using a novel logit-based <b>fairness</b> feedback model. The proposed model and learning algorithm are both validated using <b>simulation</b> experiments as well as Prolific data. Public preferences towards group <b>fairness</b> notions in the context of kidney placement have been estimated and discussed in detail. The specific ARP tested in the Prolific survey has been deemed fair by the participants.

{{</citation>}}


### (8/44 | 67/258) Exploration is Harder than Prediction: Cryptographically Separating Reinforcement Learning from Supervised Learning (Noah Golowich et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Noah Golowich, Ankur Moitra, Dhruv Rohatgi. (2024)  
**Exploration is Harder than Prediction: Cryptographically Separating Reinforcement Learning from Supervised Learning**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Exploration is Harder than Prediction: Cryptographically Separating Reinforcement Learning from Supervised Learning" index=67>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-67 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-CC, cs-CR, cs-DS, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 40  
Keywords: Markov Decision Process, Reinforcement Learning, Supervised Learning, Supervised Learning  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03774v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03774v1.pdf" filename="2404.03774v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Supervised</b> <b>learning</b> is often computationally easy in practice. But to what extent does this mean that other modes of learning, such as <b>reinforcement</b> <b>learning</b> (RL), ought to be computationally easy by extension? In this work we show the first cryptographic separation between RL and <b>supervised</b> <b>learning,</b> by exhibiting a class of block <b>MDPs</b> and associated decoding functions where reward-free exploration is provably computationally harder than the associated regression problem. We also show that there is no computationally efficient algorithm for reward-directed RL in block <b>MDPs,</b> even when given access to an oracle for this regression problem. It is known that being able to perform regression in block <b>MDPs</b> is necessary for finding a good policy; our results suggest that it is not sufficient. Our separation lower bound uses a new robustness property of the Learning Parities with Noise (LPN) hardness assumption, which is crucial in handling the dependent nature of RL data. We argue that separations and oracle lower bounds, such as ours, are a more meaningful way to prove hardness of learning because the constructions better reflect the practical reality that <b>supervised</b> <b>learning</b> by itself is often not the computational bottleneck.

{{</citation>}}

**ABSTRACT**  
This work focuses on the challenges of non-IID data and stragglers/dropouts in <b>federated</b> <b>learning.</b> We introduce and explore a privacy-flexible paradigm that models parts of the clients' local data as non-private, offering a more versatile and business-oriented perspective on privacy. Within this framework, we propose a data-driven strategy for mitigating the effects of label heterogeneity and client straggling on <b>federated</b> <b>learning.</b> Our solution combines both offline data sharing and approximate gradient coding techniques. Through numerical <b>simulations</b> using the <b>MNIST</b> dataset, we demonstrate that our approach enables achieving a deliberate trade-off between privacy and utility, leading to improved model convergence and accuracy while using an adaptable portion of non-private data.

**Knowledge-Based Convolutional Neural Network for the Simulation and Prediction of Two-Phase Darcy Flows**

<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Knowledge-Based Convolutional Neural Network for the Simulation and Prediction of Two-Phase Darcy Flows" index=69>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>

Primary Category: cs.LG

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03240v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03240v1.pdf" filename="2404.03240v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Physics-informed neural networks (PINNs) have gained significant prominence as a powerful tool in the field of scientific computing and <b>simulations.</b> Their ability to seamlessly integrate physical principles into deep learning architectures has revolutionized the approaches to solving complex problems in physics and engineering. However, a persistent challenge faced by mainstream PINNs lies in their handling of discontinuous input data, leading to inaccuracies in predictions. This study addresses these challenges by incorporating the discretized forms of the governing equations into the PINN framework. We propose to combine the power of neural networks with the dynamics imposed by the discretized differential equations. By discretizing the governing equations, the PINN learns to account for the discontinuities and accurately capture the underlying relationships between inputs and outputs, improving the accuracy compared to traditional interpolation techniques. Moreover, by leveraging the power of neural networks, the computational cost associated with numerical <b>simulations</b> is substantially reduced. We evaluate our model on a large-scale dataset for the prediction of pressure and saturation fields demonstrating high accuracies compared to non-physically aware models.

{{</citation>}}


### (11/44 | 70/258) Outlier-Efficient Hopfield Layers for Large Transformer-Based Models (Jerry Yao-Chieh Hu et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Jerry Yao-Chieh Hu, Pei-Hsuan Chang, Robin Luo, Hong-Yu Chen, Weijian Li, Wei-Po Wang, Han Liu. (2024)  
**Outlier-Efficient Hopfield Layers for Large Transformer-Based Models**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Outlier-Efficient Hopfield Layers for Large Transformer-Based Models" index=70>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-70 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-LG, cs.LG, stat-ML  
Keyword Score: 36  
Keywords: Benchmarking, Benchmarking, Hopfield Network, BERT, Transformer  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03828v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03828v1.pdf" filename="2404.03828v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
We introduce an Outlier-Efficient Modern <b>Hopfield</b> <b>Model</b> (termed $\mathtt{OutEffHop}$) and use it to address the outlier-induced challenge of quantizing gigantic <b>transformer-based</b> models. Our main contribution is a novel associative memory model facilitating \textit{outlier-efficient} associative memory retrievals. Interestingly, this memory model manifests a model-based interpretation of an outlier-efficient attention mechanism ($\text{Softmax}_1$): it is an approximation of the memory retrieval process of $\mathtt{OutEffHop}$. Methodologically, this allows us to debut novel outlier-efficient <b>Hopfield</b> <b>layers</b> a powerful attention alternative with superior post-quantization performance. Theoretically, the Outlier-Efficient Modern <b>Hopfield</b> <b>Model</b> retains and improves the desirable properties of the standard modern <b>Hopfield</b> <b>models,</b> including fixed point convergence and exponential storage capacity. Empirically, we demonstrate the proposed model's efficacy across large-scale <b>transformer-based</b> and <b>Hopfield-based</b> <b>models</b> (including <b>BERT,</b> OPT, ViT and STanHop-Net), <b>benchmarking</b> against state-of-the-art methods including $\mathtt{Clipped\_Softmax}$ and $\mathtt{Gated\_Attention}$. Notably, $\mathtt{OutEffHop}$ achieves on average $\sim$22+\% reductions in both average kurtosis and maximum infinity norm of model outputs accross 4 models.

### (12/44 | 71/258) Generalization Bounds for Message Passing Networks on Mixture of Graphons (Sohir Maskey et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Sohir Maskey, Gitta Kutyniok, Ron Levie. (2024)  
**Generalization Bounds for Message Passing Networks on Mixture of Graphons**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Generalization Bounds for Message Passing Networks on Mixture of Graphons" index=71>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-71 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 33  
Keywords: Message-Passing, Graph, Graph Neural Network, Graph Neural Network  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03473v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03473v1.pdf" filename="2404.03473v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
We study the generalization capabilities of Message Passing Neural Networks (MPNNs), a prevalent class of <b>Graph</b> <b>Neural</b> <b>Networks</b> <b>(GNN).</b> We derive generalization bounds specifically for MPNNs with normalized sum aggregation and mean aggregation. Our analysis is based on a data generation model incorporating a finite set of template graphons. Each <b>graph</b> <b>within</b> <b>this</b> framework is generated by sampling from one of the graphons with a certain degree of perturbation. In particular, we extend previous MPNN generalization results to a more realistic setting, which includes the following modifications: 1) we analyze simple random <b>graphs</b> <b>with</b> <b>Bernoulli-distributed</b> edges instead of weighted <b>graphs;</b> <b>2)</b> <b>we</b> sample both <b>graphs</b> <b>and</b> <b>graph</b> <b>signals</b> <b>from</b> perturbed graphons instead of clean graphons; and 3) we analyze sparse <b>graphs</b> <b>instead</b> <b>of</b> dense <b>graphs.</b> <b>In</b> <b>this</b> more realistic and challenging scenario, we provide a generalization bound that decreases as the average number of nodes in the <b>graphs</b> <b>increases.</b> <b>Our</b> results imply that MPNNs with higher complexity than the size of the training set can still generalize effectively, as long as the <b>graphs</b> <b>are</b> <b>sufficiently</b> large.

{{</citation>}}


### (13/44 | 72/258) On the Theoretical Expressive Power and the Design Space of Higher-Order Graph Transformers (Cai Zhou et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Cai Zhou, Rose Yu, Yusu Wang. (2024)  
**On the Theoretical Expressive Power and the Design Space of Higher-Order Graph Transformers**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="On the Theoretical Expressive Power and the Design Space of Higher-Order Graph Transformers" index=72>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>

Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-CG, cs-LG, cs.LG, math-GN  
Keyword Score: 33  
Keywords: Graph, Graph Neural Network, Transformer, Self-Attention  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03380v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03380v1.pdf" filename="2404.03380v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Graph</b> <b>transformers</b> <b>have</b> recently received significant attention in <b>graph</b> <b>learning,</b> <b>partly</b> due to their ability to capture more global interaction via <b>self-attention.</b> Nevertheless, while higher-order <b>graph</b> <b>neural</b> <b>networks</b> have been reasonably well studied, the exploration of extending <b>graph</b> <b>transformers</b> <b>to</b> higher-order variants is just starting. Both theoretical understanding and empirical results are limited. In this paper, we provide a systematic study of the theoretical expressive power of order-$k$ <b>graph</b> <b>transformers</b> <b>and</b> sparse variants. We first show that, an order-$k$ <b>graph</b> <b>transformer</b> <b>without</b> additional structural information is less expressive than the $k$-Weisfeiler Lehman ($k$-WL) test despite its high computational cost. We then explore strategies to both sparsify and enhance the higher-order <b>graph</b> <b>transformers,</b> <b>aiming</b> to improve both their efficiency and expressiveness. Indeed, sparsification based on neighborhood information can enhance the expressive power, as it provides additional information about input <b>graph</b> <b>structures.</b> <b>In</b> particular, we show that a natural neighborhood-based sparse order-$k$ <b>transformer</b> model is not only computationally efficient, but also expressive -- as expressive as $k$-WL test. We further study several other sparse <b>graph</b> <b>attention</b> <b>models</b> that are computationally efficient and provide their expressiveness analysis. Finally, we provide experimental results to show the effectiveness of the different sparsification strategies.

{{</citation>}}


### (14/44 | 73/258) Graph Neural Networks for Electric and Hydraulic Data Fusion to Enhance Short-term Forecasting of Pumped-storage Hydroelectricity (Raffael Theiler et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Raffael Theiler, Olga Fink. (2024)  
**Graph Neural Networks for Electric and Hydraulic Data Fusion to Enhance Short-term Forecasting of Pumped-storage Hydroelectricity**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Graph Neural Networks for Electric and Hydraulic Data Fusion to Enhance Short-term Forecasting of Pumped-storage Hydroelectricity" index=73>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-73 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-LG, cs-SY, cs.LG, eess-SP, eess-SY  
Keyword Score: 33  
Keywords: Graph, Graph Neural Network, Graph Neural Network, Self-Attention  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03368v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03368v1.pdf" filename="2404.03368v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Pumped-storage hydropower plants (PSH) actively participate in grid power-frequency control and therefore often operate under dynamic conditions, which results in rapidly varying system states. Predicting these dynamically changing states is essential for comprehending the underlying sensor and machine conditions. This understanding aids in detecting anomalies and faults, ensuring the reliable operation of the connected power grid, and in identifying faulty and miscalibrated sensors. PSH are complex, highly interconnected systems encompassing electrical and hydraulic subsystems, each characterized by their respective underlying networks that can individually be represented as <b>graphs.</b> <b>To</b> <b>take</b> advantage of this relational inductive bias, <b>graph</b> <b>neural</b> <b>networks</b> <b>(GNNs)</b> have been separately applied to state forecasting tasks in the individual subsystems, but without considering their interdependencies. In PSH, however, these subsystems depend on the same control input, making their operations highly interdependent and interconnected. Consequently, hydraulic and electrical sensor data should be fused across PSH subsystems to improve state forecasting accuracy. This approach has not been explored in <b>GNN</b> literature yet because many available PSH <b>graphs</b> <b>are</b> <b>limited</b> to their respective subsystem boundaries, which makes the method unsuitable to be applied directly. In this work, we introduce the application of spectral-temporal <b>graph</b> <b>neural</b> <b>networks,</b> which leverage <b>self-attention</b> mechanisms to concurrently capture and learn meaningful subsystem interdependencies and the dynamic patterns observed in electric and hydraulic sensors. Our method effectively fuses data from the PSH's subsystems by operating on a unified, system-wide <b>graph,</b> <b>learned</b> <b>directly</b> from the data, This approach leads to demonstrably improved state forecasting performance and enhanced generalizability.

{{</citation>}}


### (15/44 | 74/258) SiloFuse: Cross-silo Synthetic Data Generation with Latent Tabular Diffusion Models (Aditya Shankar et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Aditya Shankar, Hans Brouwer, Rihan Hai, Lydia Chen. (2024)  
**SiloFuse: Cross-silo Synthetic Data Generation with Latent Tabular Diffusion Models**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="SiloFuse: Cross-silo Synthetic Data Generation with Latent Tabular Diffusion Models" index=74>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-74 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-CR, cs-DB, cs-DC, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 33  
Keywords: Diffusion Model, Autoencoder, Benchmarking, Generative Adversarial Network  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03299v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03299v1.pdf" filename="2404.03299v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Synthetic tabular data is crucial for sharing and augmenting data across silos, especially for enterprises with proprietary data. However, existing synthesizers are designed for centrally stored data. Hence, they struggle with real-world scenarios where features are distributed across multiple silos, necessitating on-premise data storage. We introduce SiloFuse, a novel generative framework for high-quality synthesis from cross-silo tabular data. To ensure privacy, SiloFuse utilizes a distributed latent tabular <b>diffusion</b> <b>architecture.</b> Through <b>autoencoders,</b> latent representations are learned for each client's features, masking their actual values. We employ stacked distributed training to improve communication efficiency, reducing the number of rounds to a single step. Under SiloFuse, we prove the impossibility of data reconstruction for vertically partitioned synthesis and quantify privacy risks through three attacks using our <b>benchmark</b> framework. Experimental results on nine datasets showcase SiloFuse's competence against centralized <b>diffusion-based</b> <b>synthesizers.</b> Notably, SiloFuse achieves 43.8 and 29.8 higher percentage points over <b>GANs</b> in resemblance and utility. Experiments on communication show stacked training's fixed cost compared to the growing costs of end-to-end training as the number of training iterations increases. Additionally, SiloFuse proves robust to feature permutations and varying numbers of clients.

{{</citation>}}


### (16/44 | 75/258) Mitigating the Impact of Outlier Channels for Language Model Quantization with Activation Regularization (Aniruddha Nrusimha et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Aniruddha Nrusimha, Mayank Mishra, Naigang Wang, Dan Alistarh, Rameswar Panda, Yoon Kim. (2024)  
**Mitigating the Impact of Outlier Channels for Language Model Quantization with Activation Regularization**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Mitigating the Impact of Outlier Channels for Language Model Quantization with Activation Regularization" index=75>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-75 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-CL, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 30  
Keywords: Model Quantization, Quantization, Quantization  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03605v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03605v1.pdf" filename="2404.03605v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
We consider the problem of accurate <b>quantization</b> for language <b>models,</b> <b>where</b> both the weights and activations are uniformly <b>quantized</b> to 4 bits per parameter, the lowest bitwidth format natively supported by GPU hardware. In this context, the key challenge is activation <b>quantization:</b> it is known that language <b>models</b> <b>contain</b> outlier channels whose values on average are orders of magnitude higher than than other channels, which prevents accurate low-bitwidth <b>quantization</b> with known techniques. We systematically study this phenomena and find that these outlier channels emerge early in training, and that they occur more frequently in layers with residual streams. We then propose a simple strategy which regularizes a layer's inputs via <b>quantization-aware</b> training (QAT) and its outputs via activation kurtosis regularization. We show that regularizing both the inputs and outputs is crucial for preventing a <b>model's</b> <b>"migrating"</b> the difficulty in input <b>quantization</b> to the weights, which makes post-training <b>quantization</b> (PTQ) of weights more difficult. When combined with weight PTQ, we show that our approach can obtain a W4A4 <b>model</b> <b>that</b> performs competitively to the standard-precision W16A16 baseline.

{{</citation>}}


### (17/44 | 76/258) Self-organized arrival system for urban air mobility (Martin Waltz et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Martin Waltz, Ostap Okhrin, Michael Schultz. (2024)  
**Self-organized arrival system for urban air mobility**

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Urban air mobility is an innovative mode of transportation in which electric vertical takeoff and landing (eVTOL) vehicles operate between nodes called vertiports. We outline a self-organized vertiport arrival system based on deep <b>reinforcement</b> <b>learning.</b> The airspace around the vertiport is assumed to be circular, and the vehicles can freely operate inside. Each aircraft is considered an individual agent and follows a shared policy, resulting in decentralized actions that are based on local information. We investigate the development of the <b>reinforcement</b> <b>learning</b> policy during training and illustrate how the algorithm moves from suboptimal local holding patterns to a safe and efficient final policy. The latter is validated in <b>simulation-based</b> scenarios and also deployed on small-scale unmanned aerial vehicles to showcase its real-world usability.

{{</citation>}}


### (18/44 | 77/258) Investigating the Robustness of Counterfactual Learning to Rank Models: A Reproducibility Study (Zechun Niu et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Zechun Niu, Jiaxin Mao, Qingyao Ai, Ji-Rong Wen. (2024)  
**Investigating the Robustness of Counterfactual Learning to Rank Models: A Reproducibility Study**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Investigating the Robustness of Counterfactual Learning to Rank Models: A Reproducibility Study" index=77>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-77 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.LG  
Categories: cs-AI, cs-IR, cs-LG, cs.LG  
Keyword Score: 30  
Keywords: Counter-factual, Simulation, Simulator  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03707v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03707v1.pdf" filename="2404.03707v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Counterfactual</b> learning to rank (CLTR) has attracted extensive attention in the IR community for its ability to leverage massive logged user interaction data to train ranking models. While the CLTR models can be theoretically unbiased when the user behavior assumption is correct and the propensity estimation is accurate, their effectiveness is usually empirically evaluated via <b>simulation-based</b> experiments due to a lack of widely-available, large-scale, real click logs. However, the mainstream <b>simulation-based</b> experiments are somewhat limited as they often feature a single, deterministic production ranker and simplified user <b>simulation</b> models to generate the synthetic click logs. As a result, the robustness of CLTR models in complex and diverse situations is largely unknown and needs further investigation. To address this problem, in this paper, we aim to investigate the robustness of existing CLTR models in a reproducibility study with extensive <b>simulation-based</b> experiments that (1) use both deterministic and stochastic production rankers, each with different ranking performance, and (2) leverage multiple user <b>simulation</b> models with different user behavior assumptions. We find that the DLA models and IPS-DCM show better robustness under various <b>simulation</b> settings than IPS-PBM and PRS with offline propensity estimation. Besides, the existing CLTR models often fail to outperform the naive click baselines when the production ranker has relatively high ranking performance or certain randomness, which suggests an urgent need for developing new CLTR algorithms that work for these settings.

{{</citation>}}


### (19/44 | 78/258) Improvement of Performance in Freezing of Gait detection in Parkinsons Disease using Transformer networks and a single waist worn triaxial accelerometer (Luis Sigcha et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Luis Sigcha, Luigi Borzì, Ignacio Pavón, Nélson Costa, Susana Costa, Pedro Arezes, Juan-Manuel López, Guillermo De Arcas. (2024)  
**Improvement of Performance in Freezing of Gait detection in Parkinsons Disease using Transformer networks and a single waist worn triaxial accelerometer**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Improvement of Performance in Freezing of Gait detection in Parkinsons Disease using Transformer networks and a single waist worn triaxial accelerometer" index=78>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>

<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03704v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
