---
Primary Category: cs.DS  
Categories: cs-CC, cs-DS, cs.DS  
Keyword Score: 3  
Keywords: Graph  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03812v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03812v1.pdf" filename="2404.03812v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
For an integer $k\geq 1$, the objective of \textsc{$k$-Geodesic Center} is to find a set $\mathcal{C}$ of $k$ isometric paths such that the maximum distance between any vertex $v$ and $\mathcal{C}$ is minimised. Introduced by Gromov, \emph{$\delta$-hyperbolicity} measures how treelike a <b>graph</b> is from a metric point of view. Our main contribution in this paper is to provide an additive $O(\delta)$-approximation algorithm for \textsc{$k$-Geodesic Center} on $\delta$-hyperbolic <b>graphs.</b> On the way, we define a coarse version of the pairing property introduced by Gerstel \& Zaks (Networks, 1994) and show it holds for $\delta$-hyperbolic <b>graphs.</b> This result allows to reduce the \textsc{$k$-Geodesic Center} problem to its rooted counterpart, a main idea behind our algorithm. We also adapt a technique of Dragan \& Leitert, (TCS, 2017) to show that for every $k\geq 1$, $k$-\textsc{Geodesic Center} is NP-hard even on partial grids.

{{</citation>}}


### (2/2 | 254/258) Lower bounds for graph reconstruction with maximal independent set queries (Lukas Michel et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Lukas Michel, Alex Scott. (2024)  
**Lower bounds for graph reconstruction with maximal independent set queries**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Lower bounds for graph reconstruction with maximal independent set queries" index=254>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-254 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.DS  
Categories: cs-DS, cs.DS, math-CO  
Keyword Score: 3  
Keywords: Graph  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03472v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03472v1.pdf" filename="2404.03472v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
We investigate the number of maximal independent set queries required to reconstruct the edges of a hidden <b>graph.</b> We show that randomised adaptive algorithms need at least $\Omega(\Delta^2 \log(n / \Delta) / \log \Delta)$ queries to reconstruct $n$-vertex <b>graphs</b> of maximum degree $\Delta$ with success probability at least $1/2$, and we further improve this lower bound to $\Omega(\Delta^2 \log(n / \Delta))$ for randomised non-adaptive algorithms. We also prove that deterministic non-adaptive algorithms require at least $\Omega(\Delta^3 \log n / \log \Delta)$ queries. This improves bounds of Konrad, O'Sullivan, and Traistaru, and answers one of their questions. The proof of the lower bound for deterministic non-adaptive algorithms relies on a connection to cover-free families, for which we also improve known bounds.

{{</citation>}}


## cs.CG (2)



### (1/2 | 255/258) The Maximum Clique Problem in a Disk Graph Made Easy (J. Mark Keil et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

J. Mark Keil, Debajyoti Mondal. (2024)  
**The Maximum Clique Problem in a Disk Graph Made Easy**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="The Maximum Clique Problem in a Disk Graph Made Easy" index=255>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-255 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.CG  
Categories: 52C99, 68Q25, F-2-2; I-3-5, cs-CG, cs-DS, cs.CG  
Keyword Score: 3  
Keywords: Graph  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03751v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03751v1.pdf" filename="2404.03751v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
A disk <b>graph</b> is an intersection <b>graph</b> of disks in $\mathbb{R}^2$. Determining the computational complexity of finding a maximum clique in a disk <b>graph</b> is a long-standing open problem. In 1990, Clark, Colbourn, and Johnson gave a polynomial-time algorithm for computing a maximum clique in a unit disk <b>graph.</b> However, finding a maximum clique when disks are of arbitrary size is widely believed to be a challenging open problem. The problem is open even if we restrict the disks to have at most two different sizes of radii, or restrict the radii to be within $[1,1+\varepsilon]$ for some $\epsilon>0$. In this paper, we provide a new perspective to examine adjacencies in a disk <b>graph</b> that helps obtain the following results. - We design an $O(2^k n^{2k} poly(n))$-time algorithm to find a maximum clique in a $n$-vertex disk <b>graph</b> with $k$ different sizes of radii. This is polynomial for every fixed $k$, and thus settles the open question for the case when $k=2$. - Given a set of $n$ unit disks, we show how to compute a maximum clique inside each possible axis-aligned rectangle determined by the disk centers in $O(n^5\log n)$-time. This is at least a factor of $n^{4/3}$ faster than applying the fastest known algorithm for finding a maximum clique in a unit disk <b>graph</b> for each rectangle independently. - We give an $O(2^kn^{2rk} poly(n,r))$-time algorithm to find a maximum clique in a $n$-vertex ball <b>graph</b> with $k$ different sizes of radii where the ball centers lie on $r$ parallel planes. This is polynomial for every fixed $k$ and $r$, and thus contrasts the previously known NP-hardness result for finding a maximum clique in an arbitrary ball <b>graph.</b>

{{</citation>}}


### (2/2 | 256/258) Improved Total Domination and Total Roman Domination in Unit Disk Graphs (Sasmita Rout et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Sasmita Rout, Gautam Kumar Das. (2024)  
**Improved Total Domination and Total Roman Domination in Unit Disk Graphs**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Improved Total Domination and Total Roman Domination in Unit Disk Graphs" index=256>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-256 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.CG  
Categories: cs-CG, cs.CG, math-CO  
Keyword Score: 3  
Keywords: Graph  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03511v1" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03511v1.pdf" filename="2404.03511v1.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Let $G=(V, E)$ be a simple undirected <b>graph</b> with no isolated vertex. A set $D_t\subseteq V$ is a total dominating set of $G$ if $(i)$ $D_t$ is a dominating set, and $(ii)$ the set $D_t$ induces a subgraph with no isolated vertex. The total dominating set of minimum cardinality is called the minimum total dominating set, and the size of the minimum total dominating set is called the total domination number ($\gamma_t(G)$). Given a <b>graph</b> $G$, the total dominating set (TDS) problem is to find a total dominating set of minimum cardinality. A Roman dominating function (RDF) on a <b>graph</b> $G$ is a function $f:V\rightarrow \{0,1,2\}$ such that each vertex $v\in V$ with $f(v)=0$ is adjacent to at least one vertex $u\in V$ with $f(u)=2$. A RDF $f$ of a <b>graph</b> $G$ is said to be a total Roman dominating function (TRDF) if the induced subgraph of $V_1\cup V_2$ does not contain any isolated vertex, where $V_i=\{u\in V|f(u)=i\}$. Given a <b>graph</b> $G$, the total Roman dominating set (TRDS) problem is to minimize the weight, $W(f)=\sum_{u\in V} f(u)$, called the total Roman domination number ($\gamma_{tR}(G)$). In this paper, we are the first to show that the TRDS problem is NP-complete in unit disk <b>graphs</b> (UDGs). Furthermore, we propose a $7.17\operatorname{-}$ factor approximation algorithm for the TDS problem and a $6.03\operatorname{-}$ factor approximation algorithm for the TRDS problem in geometric unit disk <b>graphs.</b> The running time for both algorithms is notably bounded by $O(n\log{k})$, where $n$ represents the number of vertices in the given UDG and $k$ represents the size of the independent set in (i.e., $D$ and $V_2$ in TDS and TRDS problems, respectively) the given UDG.

{{</citation>}}


## cs.DB (1)



### (1/1 | 257/258) Reservoir Sampling over Joins (Binyang Dai et al., 2024)

{{<citation>}}

Binyang Dai, Xiao Hu, Ke Yi. (2024)  
**Reservoir Sampling over Joins**
<br/>
<button class="copy-to-clipboard" title="Reservoir Sampling over Joins" index=257>
  <span class="copy-to-clipboard-item">Copy Title<span>
</button>
<div class="toast toast-copied toast-index-257 align-items-center text-bg-secondary border-0 position-absolute top-0 end-0" role="alert" aria-live="assertive" aria-atomic="true">
  <div class="d-flex">
    <div class="toast-body">
      Copied!
    </div>
  </div>
</div>

---
Primary Category: cs.DB  
Categories: cs-DB, cs.DB  
Keyword Score: 3  
Keywords: Graph  
<a type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary" href="http://arxiv.org/abs/2404.03194v2" target="_blank" >Paper Link</a>
<button type="button" class="btn btn-outline-primary download-pdf" url="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2404.03194v2.pdf" filename="2404.03194v2.pdf">Download PDF</button>

---


**ABSTRACT**  
Sampling over joins is a fundamental task in large-scale data analytics. Instead of computing the full join results, which could be massive, a uniform sample of the join results would suffice for many purposes, such as answering analytical queries or training machine learning models. In this paper, we study the problem of how to maintain a random sample over joins while the tuples are streaming in. Without the join, this problem can be solved by some simple and classical reservoir sampling algorithms. However, the join operator makes the problem significantly harder, as the join size can be polynomially larger than the input. We present a new algorithm for this problem that achieves a near-linear complexity. The key technical components are a generalized reservoir sampling algorithm that supports a predicate, and a dynamic index for sampling over joins. We also conduct extensive experiments on both <b>graph</b> and relational data over various join queries, and the experimental results demonstrate significant performance improvement over the state of the art.

{{</citation>}}

### (1/1 | 258/258) TEGRA -- Scaling Up Terascale Graph Processing with Disaggregated Computing (William Shaddix et al., 2024)

**ABSTRACT**  
<b>Graphs</b> are essential for representing relationships in various domains, driving modern AI applications such as <b>graph</b> analytics and neural networks across science, engineering, cybersecurity, transportation, and economics. However, the size of modern <b>graphs</b> are rapidly expanding, posing challenges for traditional CPUs and GPUs in meeting real-time processing demands. As a result, hardware accelerators for <b>graph</b> processing have been proposed. However, the largest <b>graphs</b> that can be handled by these systems is still modest often targeting Twitter graph(1.4B edges approximately). This paper aims to address this limitation by developing a <b>graph</b> accelerator capable of terascale <b>graph</b> processing. Scale out architectures, architectures where nodes are replicated to expand to larger datasets, are natural for handling larger <b>graphs.</b> We argue that this approach is not appropriate for very large-scale <b>graphs</b> because it leads to under utilization of both memory resources and compute resources. Additionally, vertex and edge processing have different access patterns. Communication overheads also pose further challenges in designing scalable architectures. To overcome these issues, this paper proposes TEGRA, a scale-up architecture for terascale <b>graph</b> processing. TEGRA leverages a composable computing system with disaggregated resources and a communication architecture inspired by Active Messages. By employing direct communication between cores and optimizing memory interconnect utilization, TEGRA effectively reduces communication overhead and improves resource utilization, therefore enabling efficient processing of terascale <b>graphs.</b>
